25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n13586-1" target="دِينَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n13589"/></foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">دَيْنٌ</foreign> (T, M, K) in the sense above explained: (K:) a valid <foreign lang="ar">دَينْ</foreign> (<foreign lang="ar">دَينٌ صَحِيحٌ</foreign>) is <hi rend="ital">such as does not become annulled save by payment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by one's being declared clear,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quit:</hi> compensation in the case of a contract which a slave makes with his owner to pay him a certain sum as the price of himself and on the payment thereof to be free is not a valid <foreign lang="ar">دَيْن</foreign>, because it may become annulled without payment, and without his being declared clear, or quit; that is, by the slave's being unable to pay it: (KT:) in the language of the law, but not in the proper language, <foreign lang="ar">دَيْنٌ</foreign> is also applied to <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">a debt incurred by</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a thing taken unjustly, injuriously,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by violence;</hi> as being likened to a <foreign lang="ar">دَيْن</foreign> properly so called: (Msb:) and it signifies also <hi rend="ital">anything that is not present:</hi> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">anything to be paid,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">done, at a future time:</hi>] (M, K:) the pl.                   </form>, applied to a man, (S, M, K,) and also to a woman, (M, K,) without <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, (M,) One <hi rend="ital">who gives,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grants, loans,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like,</hi> (Sh, T, M, K,) <hi rend="ital">to men,</hi> (M,) <hi rend="ital">much,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">often;</hi> (Sh, T, K:) and also, (Sh, T, K,) if you will, (Sh, T,) one <hi rend="ital">who seeks,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demands, loans,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, much,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">often:</hi> (Sh, T, K:) thus bearing two contr. significations: (K:) or <hi rend="ital">one whose custom it is to take,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">receive, by incurring debt,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to buy upon credit;</hi> and, <hi rend="ital">to seek,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demand, loans,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like:</hi> (S:) or it is an intensive epithet, signifying one <hi rend="ital">having</hi> [<hi rend="ital">many</hi>] <hi rend="ital">debts:</hi> (IAth, TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">مَدَايِينُ</foreign>, (M, K,) masc. and fem.
